(a) Will he inform this House -

(i) the number of water supply projects implemented in the Badulla District up to now since the present Good Governance Government came to power in 2015;

(ii) separately, the name and number of beneficiaries of each of the aforesaid water supply projects along with the amount of money spent on each project; and

(iii) the steps expected to be taken to remedy the drinking water issue of the people of Badulla?

( ) ' , '? asked the Prime Minister and Minister of National Policies and Economic Affairs:

(a) Will he admit that-

(i) the traditional gem miners in the Ratnapura District, the leading district in the gem industry that provides a significant contribution to the national income, are losing that industry; and

(ii) the reason for this situation is that the traditional miner has fallen into the state of a labourer among the businessmen who are engaged in large-scale businesses within this industry?

(b) Will he inform this House-

(i) whether licences have been issued to use backhoes in large-scale mining industry;

(ii) if so, the names and addresses of licence holders;

(iii) whether he admits that using of backhoes for traditional mining causes an injustice to the traditional miners as well as severe environmental damages; and

(iv) the measures that can be taken to prevent this situation?

(c) If not, why? & . &G (;2 8 * ) (The Hon. Gayantha Karunatileka) N L@, 7L c cSc j UL 7L &$  L .

() ' , '? asked the Minister of Plantation Industries:

(a) Will he inform this House -

(i) whether he is aware that a subsidy called Kapruk Purawara was provided to coconut farmers as Rs. 52 per tree from 8 trees up to 5 acres and that the said subsidy is not provided at present; and

(ii) whether he admits that eventhough the coconut cultivators who did not receive the subsidy handed over applications to the Office of the Coconut Cultivation Board at Ratnapura in December 2016 requesting that subsidy , no response has been received up to now?

(b) Will he also inform this House whether immediate action would be taken after looking into this matter, to provide that subsidy to the coconut farmers?

, #'$LE @ 23(2) S . N B$ w . '(* + ,. 0  7 QUESTION BY PRIVATE NOTICE #$ *. + |, $ $ NON-ISSUANCE OF ADVERSE WEATHER WARNING & F.  (;2 M 20) (The Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena) N L@, I pose this question to the Hon. Prime Minister or the Minister of Disaster Management.

On 29th of November, Sri Lanka was badly affected by a disastrous tropical storm which had caused at least 14 deaths so far and destroyed roofs of houses and power lines. Despite warnings being received from overseas at least three days ahead, the Government agencies ignored them only issuing an advisory to the fishing community. This not only affected the people, caused severe damage to property and the economy of the country, but it is likely to tarnish the reputation of the country in the tourism industry and commerce, leading to a decline in the relevant industries.

This shows the apathy of the Government in the face of disasters and exemplifies the tardiness. (1) Will the Hon. Prime Minister explain to the House why international warnings were ignored and the public was left unaware of the impending disaster?

(2) What action does the Government intend to take to face future storms, bearing in mind that the people affected by earlier floods are still awaiting adequate compensation and what measures will be taken to alleviate the suffering of those affected by such weather conditions?

Sir, yesterday's The Sunday Times reports, I quote, One depression gone, but another on the way, giving all the details of Cyclone Ockhi. Sir, I table* that article.

Why is that Report not tabled in Parliament by the Hon. Prime Minister? When we debated that issue, it was promised that the Report will be submitted. It is lying in the Headquarters of the Army Commander.

[ $ ,C S NQ +$$x ,$ .  57  S  c. 2016 \ [@B O $) $ b B# , c - "WHO certifies Sri Lanka as free of malaria lymphatic filariasis and validates maternal and neonatal tetanus elimination in 2016. The Action Plan for Non-Communicable Diseases and the regions first NCD Alliance has been launched. Sri Lanka has become the first country in the region to mandate sugar content labels on sugary drinks as a diabetic prevention measure. The tax on tobacco products has been increased to 90 per cent of the retail price, one of the highest. Maximum prices have been fixed for 48 essential medicines to ensure their affordability."

[12.20 p.m.] & (J) . x5. (;2 ( ) . ) (The Hon. (Dr.) S. Sivamohan) Thank you very much, Hon. Chairman, for giving me the opportunity to speak. I want to express my views on some estimates done by the World Health Organization. Sri Lanka's expenditure on health, both public and private, was around 3.2 per cent of the Gross Domestic Product - GDP - or US Dollars 89 per head in 2012. Life expectancy has raised from around 60 years in 1960 to 74 years in 2012 according to the World Bank statistics. In Sri Lanka, the mortality rate of children under 5 years has fallen from 9.8 deaths per 1,000 live births to 9.6 deaths per 1,000 live births in 2013. These are good health indicators.

I wish to thank the present Minister of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine, Hon. (Dr.) Rajitha Senaratne and at the same time, the former Minister of Health, President His Excellency Maithripala Sirisena, for the valuable efforts taken to improve the health sector in this country. The success of Sri Lankas health sector is largely due to its effective public delivery system, which provides both preventive and curative care at low cost. Government provides healthcare free for all citizens and accounts for almost all preventive care and most in-patient treatment. However, the public health sector has inadequate capacity, limited access to specialist treatment and inconsistent service standards.

Member, just to keep you informed, for 2018, Rs. 3 billion, that is, Rs. 3,000 million or Rs. 30,000 lakhs, has been allocated by our Government only for the North and the East to provide housing. So, that is a large chunk of money that we are investing to help the people of the North and the East.  -  % +   !. & 8 @ (;2  ) (The Hon. Sajith Premadasa) Hon. Member, I want to clarify two issues. One issue is, if grama niladaris or any other government officials are involved in embezzling funds, then I think it is a serious matter and you should take that up with the relevant line Ministries and make necessary complaints. So that, that kind of activity is prevented.

The second issue is, as far as selecting the beneficiaries for housing is concerned, we do not decide who get the houses. The Ministry of Housing and Construction does not decide who the recipients are. It is decided by the relevant District and Divisional Housing Committees where the representatives of the people, like you, can get involved and make sure that those who are most needed will receive housing. So, it is up to you to participate at the District and Divisional Housing Committees and make your recommendations in order to accommodate the wishes of those who most need housing.

Ministry of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine to the Eastern Province. [7.02 p.m.] & qf x ('J, 5 ( J 5J J%) (;2  ) - ), )  *" 0) (The Hon. Faizal Cassim - Deputy Minister of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine) Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem.

Hon. Chairman, I am very happy to speak on the Votes of the Ministry of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine and the Ministry of Housing and Construction.

First of all, I want to thank my Hon. Minister, who is dedicated, and the staff. I thank the Hon. Minister, for he never interferes with my work. He has given me freedom to work and develop the health sector in Sri Lanka.

I also wish to thank our former Secretary, Mr. Anura Jayawickrama, who gave us a helping hand in a big way in our work at the Ministry of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine, the present Secretary, Mr. Janaka Sugathadasa, the former Director-General of Health Services, Dr. Jayasundara Bandara, who left our services last week, the newly appointed Director-General of Health Services, Dr. Anil Jasinghe, a very experienced officer who has been with us, and I hope that he will carry on with his good work in the future too, the Deputy Directors-General, the Directors and all other officers. I have to thank them because they have been helpful to me in developing the health sector during the past few years.

I also have to thank the Hon. Minister of Housing and Construction, the Hon. Sajith Premadasa, for having given 20 to 50 houses for people in Pottuvil.

& || 1 (;2 ! ) (The Hon. Mohamed Navavi) Hon. Chairman, as the Hon. Minister promised, we got 57 nurses today and will get 18 doctors later. Thank you very much, Hon. Minister. & qf x (;2  )) (The Hon. Faizal Cassim) Also, we have given about Rs. 41 million only for the Puttalam Hospital. In addition to that, we have developed a lot of clinical centres in the Kalpitiya area. So we have spent more than Rs. 100 million in these areas. According to the estimates, the Hon. Minister has given Rs. 530 million for the Eastern Province. But, to my knowledge, I have been given more than Rs. 331 million. We have given Rs. 181 million for the Ampara Distirct, Rs. 80 million for Batticaloa District and Rs. 30 million for Trincomalee District to develop those areas. We are going to do more development work this year too. I thank the Hon. Minister for giving us an Accident and Emergency Treatment Unit worth of Rs. 1,800 million for Kalmunai Base Hospital. Tenders have already been called for and it is going through the TEC process. Very soon, when the Minister is going to open the A&E Building at Kalmunai North, we are going to lay foundation stone for that too.

Then, the Hon. S. Shritharan spoke about malnutrition. Nuwara Eliya is the badly affected area with malnutrition which is about 32 per cent. In Kandy, it is around 26 per cent; in Kegalle, it is 23 per cent and in Kilinochchi it is 21 per cent. I do not know from where the Hon. Member got his statistics. Anyway, according to the statistics, Nuwara Eliya is the badly affected area with malnutrition. In Nuwara Eliya it is 32 percent whereas in Kilinochchi it is 21 per cent. Anyway, we are trying our best to develop the areas which are badly affected by malnutrition. Then, malnutrition, in Hambantota it is about 25 per cent; in Monaragala and Matale it is 10 per cent; in & G% (;2 0 0$) (The Hon. Chairman) Hon. Deputy Minister, your time is over. Please, wind up now because the Hon. Minister would want ten minutes for the Reply. & qf x (;2  )) (The Hon. Faizal Cassim) Okay. Give me five more minutes. I have little more to explain and then I will wind up. & G% (;2 0 0$) (The Hon. Chairman) We can give you about two more minutes. & qf x (;2  )) (The Hon. Faizal Cassim) I thank the Hon. Minister once again. When he visited Nintavur area, I made a request for a regional

2761 2762

He has also given more bank loans to the people in my district and I have to thank him for that also. Further, I have to thank Mr. M.R. Jeyachandran, the Director General of the Buildings Department, and his team for giving me their fullest support to finish our contracts through the Ministry.

My Hon. Minister left out some points in making his speech. This year, we have been spending around Rs. 200 million on the estate sector. In Badulla and Nuwara Eliya Districts, almost 95 per cent of the work has been finished. They have promised to finish the balance 5 per cent of the work before the end of December, this year. Next year, we have asked the development officers in the estate sector to go around Kalutara, Galle, Matara and Matale Districts, do a survey with the help of the Buildings Department and provide us with information as to the balance work that needs to be done next year.

We want to develop the estate sector in Sri Lanka, which has been badly affected, health-wise and to improve the lives of the people. My Minister has already instructed to bring another 200 estate hospitals under our Ministry. He has already requested the Secretary to the Ministry to prepare a Cabinet Paper in that regard so that those hospitals will also be brought under us and we can develop them in the future.

Recently, I asked a French NGO to come and meet me - the Hon. Mano Ganesan was also with me on that day - and I told them that we have developed all the infrastructure and that we only need doctors now. I asked the NGO, if possible, to pay the retired doctors, whose services could be obtained to treat those people. Normally, those areas are covered by doctors, but due to the shortage of doctors, the service provided is unsatisfactory. So, we are hoping to take in some more doctors and if this NGO can help us to get those doctors, it would be more helpful for the people.

Sir, in the Ampara Hospital, we have already opened up a paying ward. The Hon. Minister opened it. In the last Budget, we proposed to build a ward complex with a pediatric unit. Then, when the Hon. Minister visited Ampara, he gave a promise to build a cath lab also in the Ampara Hospital. I must thank the Hon. Minister for that.

About two months back, the Hon. Minister visited my village, Nintavur, to open an Osu Sala outlet, which is very helpful to the public. We are planning to open some more Osu Sala outlets in Tirukovil, Samanthurai, Kaluwanchikudy, Mahaladitivu, Eravur and Valaichenai where the hospitals are situated. I am sorry, earlier, I forgot to thank the Chairman, SPC and his Managing Director too. We want to open more Osu Sala outlets with more space.

The Hon. Navavi is here. Hon. Member, to my knowledge, we have spent more than Rs. 100 million for the development of the Puttalam Base Hospital and the Kalpitiya area. We have already done our master plan. As requested, our Hon. Minister instructed to construct some buildings which have not been built by the Provincial Council.

Child and Maternity Hospital. He told me that work can immediately be commenced, and funds have been allocated in the Budget for that. Further, we have planned to merge the Akkaraipattu Base Hospital with Palamunai Hospital because Akkaraipattu Hospital does not have enough space. Also, we are planning to establish an eye hospital and an OMF dental hospital in this area too. I table* all these documents to be included in the Hansard.

Sir, as regards indigenous medicine sector, an eight-storeyed ward complex for Borella Ayurvedic Teaching Hospital with a total cost Rs. 1,113 million will be completed next year. A traditional Ayurvedic Hospital is going to be established at a total cost of Rs. 180 million at Wedagama in Gampaha District with the aim of providing traditional treatment. Also, steps have been taken to establish a new Ayurvedic Hospital at Nintavur in Ampara District at a total cost of Rs. 186 million.

Also a Siddha Medicine Teaching Hospital will be established in Trincomalee. The estimated cost for that hospital is Rs. 575 million. A Post Graduate Institute of Indigenous Medicine will also be established in 2018. Rs. 225 million has already been allocated in 2017 and the balance of Rs. 40 million is allocated in 2018.

Sir, I can provide a lot of information about what we have been doing these days for the development of the health sector. After the Hon. Minister took over this Ministry, he has dedicatedly been working to develop the health sector. All of us have been speaking about it throughout the whole day. You have done a lot of good things.
